</tr><tr><td style="text-align:right;font-size:115%;padding-top: 0.6em;"><div class="plainlinks hlist navbar mini"><ul><li class="nv-view"><a href="/wiki/Template:Green_politics" title="Template:Green politics"><abbr title="View this template">v</abbr></a></li><li class="nv-talk"><a href="/wiki/Template_talk:Green_politics" title="Template talk:Green politics"><abbr title="Discuss this template">t</abbr></a></li><li class="nv-edit"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Template:Green_politics&amp;action=edit"><abbr title="Edit this template">e</abbr></a></li></ul></div></td></tr></tbody></table>
<p>The <b>Green Party of England and Wales</b> (<b>GPEW</b>; <a href="/wiki/Welsh_language" title="Welsh language">Welsh</a>: <i lang="cy">Plaid Werdd Cymru a Lloegr</i>) is a <a href="/wiki/Green_politics" title="Green politics">green</a>, <a href="/wiki/Left-wing_politics" title="Left-wing politics">left-wing</a> <a href="/wiki/List_of_political_parties_in_the_United_Kingdom" title="List of political parties in the United Kingdom">political party in England and Wales</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-independent.co.uk_7-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-independent.co.uk-7">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-EUROPP_8-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-EUROPP-8">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup> Headquartered in <a href="/wiki/London" title="London">London</a>, since September 2018, its co-leaders are <a href="/wiki/Si%C3%A2n_Berry" title="Siân Berry">Siân Berry</a> and <a href="/wiki/Jonathan_Bartley" title="Jonathan Bartley">Jonathan Bartley</a>. The Green Party has one representative in the <a href="/wiki/House_of_Commons_of_the_United_Kingdom" title="House of Commons of the United Kingdom">House of Commons</a>, two in the <a href="/wiki/House_of_Lords" title="House of Lords">House of Lords</a>, and seven in the <a href="/wiki/European_Parliament" title="European Parliament">European Parliament</a>. In addition, it has various councillors in <a href="/wiki/Local_government_in_the_United_Kingdom" title="Local government in the United Kingdom">UK local government</a> and two members of the <a href="/wiki/London_Assembly" title="London Assembly">London Assembly</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-gwydir_11-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-gwydir-11">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Elections_12-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Elections-12">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-brumpost_13-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-brumpost-13">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-solihull_14-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-solihull-14">&#91;14&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The party's ideology combines <a href="/wiki/Environmentalism" title="Environmentalism">environmentalism</a> with left-wing and centre-left economic policies, including well-funded, locally controlled public services within the confines of a <a href="/wiki/Steady_state_economy" class="mw-redirect" title="Steady state economy">steady state economy</a> with regulated capitalism, and supports <a href="/wiki/Proportional_representation" title="Proportional representation">proportional representation</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-15" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-15">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup> It also takes a <a href="/wiki/Progressivism#Contemporary_mainstream_political_conception" title="Progressivism">progressive</a> approach to social policies such as <a href="/wiki/Civil_liberties" title="Civil liberties">civil liberties</a>, <a href="/wiki/Animal_rights" title="Animal rights">animal rights</a>, <a href="/wiki/LGBT_rights_in_the_United_Kingdom" title="LGBT rights in the United Kingdom">LGBT rights</a> and <a href="/wiki/Drug_policy_reform" title="Drug policy reform">drug policy reform</a>. The party also believes strongly in <a href="/wiki/Nonviolence" title="Nonviolence">nonviolence</a>, <a href="/wiki/Basic_income" title="Basic income">basic income</a>, a <a href="/wiki/Living_wage" title="Living wage">living wage</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-£10_Minimum_Wage_16-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-£10_Minimum_Wage-16">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Democracy" title="Democracy">democratic</a> participation.<sup id="cite_ref-CoreValues_17-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CoreValues-17">&#91;17&#93;</a></sup> The party comprises various regional divisions, including the semi-autonomous <a href="/wiki/Wales_Green_Party" title="Wales Green Party">Wales Green Party</a>. Internationally, the party is affiliated to the <a href="/wiki/Global_Greens" title="Global Greens">Global Greens</a> and the <a href="/wiki/European_Green_Party" title="European Green Party">European Green Party</a>.
</p><p>The Green Party of England and Wales was established in 1990 alongside the <a href="/wiki/Scottish_Green_Party" title="Scottish Green Party">Scottish Green Party</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Green_Party_in_Northern_Ireland" title="Green Party in Northern Ireland">Green Party in Northern Ireland</a> through the division of the pre-existing <a href="/wiki/Green_Party_(UK)" title="Green Party (UK)">Green Party</a>, a group which had originally been established as the <a href="/wiki/PEOPLE_Party" title="PEOPLE Party">PEOPLE Party</a> in 1973. Experiencing centralising reforms spearheaded by the <a href="/wiki/Green_2000" title="Green 2000">Green 2000</a> group in the early 1990s, the party sought to emphasise growth in local governance, doing so throughout the 1990s. In 2010, the party gained its first MP in former leader <a href="/wiki/Caroline_Lucas" title="Caroline Lucas">Caroline Lucas</a>, who represents the constituency of <a href="/wiki/Brighton_Pavilion_(UK_Parliament_constituency)" title="Brighton Pavilion (UK Parliament constituency)">Brighton Pavilion</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-BBC-election2010-brightonpavillion_18-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BBC-election2010-brightonpavillion-18">&#91;18&#93;</a></sup>
</p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Green_Party_of_England_and_Wales&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: History">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/History_of_the_Green_Party_of_England_and_Wales" title="History of the Green Party of England and Wales">History of the Green Party of England and Wales</a></div>
<h3><span id="Origins_.281972.E2.80.931990.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Origins_(1972–1990)">Origins (1972–1990)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Green_Party_of_England_and_Wales&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Origins (1972–1990)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The Green Party of England and Wales has its origins in the <a href="/wiki/PEOPLE_Party" title="PEOPLE Party">PEOPLE Party</a>, which was founded in <a href="/wiki/Coventry" title="Coventry">Coventry</a>, <a href="/wiki/Warwickshire" title="Warwickshire">Warwickshire</a>, in February 1972.<sup id="cite_ref-19" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-19">&#91;19&#93;</a></sup> PEOPLE was renamed <a href="/wiki/The_Ecology_Party" class="mw-redirect" title="The Ecology Party">The Ecology Party</a> in 1975,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTERootes199566Birch200954_20-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTERootes199566Birch200954-20">&#91;20&#93;</a></sup> and in 1985 changed again to the <a href="/wiki/Green_Party_(UK)" title="Green Party (UK)">Green Party</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMcCulloch1992421Birch200954_21-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMcCulloch1992421Birch200954-21">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup> In 1989 the party's Scottish branch split to establish the independent <a href="/wiki/Scottish_Green_Party" title="Scottish Green Party">Scottish Green Party</a>, with an independent <a href="/wiki/Green_Party_in_Northern_Ireland" title="Green Party in Northern Ireland">Green Party in Northern Ireland</a> developing shortly after, leaving those branches in England and Wales to form their own party.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBirch200954_22-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBirch200954-22">&#91;22&#93;</a></sup> The Green Party of England and Wales is registered with the <a href="/wiki/Electoral_Commission_(United_Kingdom)" title="Electoral Commission (United Kingdom)">Electoral Commission</a> as simply the Green Party.<sup id="cite_ref-ECregister_23-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ECregister-23">&#91;23&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In the <a href="/wiki/1989_European_Parliament_election_in_the_United_Kingdom" title="1989 European Parliament election in the United Kingdom">1989 European Parliament elections</a>, the Green Party of England and Wales polled 15% of the vote with 2.3 million votes, the best ever performance of a Green party in a nationwide election.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEPattieRussellJohnston1991286McCulloch1992422Rootes199568–69Burchell2000145Birch200954_24-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEPattieRussellJohnston1991286McCulloch1992422Rootes199568–69Burchell2000145Birch200954-24">&#91;24&#93;</a></sup> This gave it the third largest share of the vote after the <a href="/wiki/Conservative_Party_(UK)" title="Conservative Party (UK)">Conservative</a> and <a href="/wiki/Labour_Party_(UK)" title="Labour Party (UK)">Labour</a> parties, although because of the <a href="/wiki/First-past-the-post_voting" title="First-past-the-post voting">first-past-the-post voting</a> system it failed to gain a <a href="/wiki/Member_of_the_European_Parliament" title="Member of the European Parliament">Member of the European Parliament</a> (MEP).<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEPattieRussellJohnston1991286Birch200954_25-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEPattieRussellJohnston1991286Birch200954-25">&#91;25&#93;</a></sup> This success has been attributed to both the increased respectability of environmentalism and the effects of the development boom in southern England in the late 1980s.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTERootes199569–72_26-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTERootes199569–72-26">&#91;26&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span id="Early_years:_1990.E2.80.932008"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Early_years:_1990–2008">Early years: 1990–2008</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Green_Party_of_England_and_Wales&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Early years: 1990–2008">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Seeking to capitalise on the Greens' success in the EP elections, a group named <a href="/wiki/Green_2000" title="Green 2000">Green 2000</a> was established in July 1990, arguing for an internal reorganisation of the party in order to develop it into an effective electoral force capable of securing seats in the House of Commons.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMcCulloch1992422Burchell2000145_27-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMcCulloch1992422Burchell2000145-27">&#91;27&#93;</a></sup> Its proposed reforms included a more centralised structure, the replacement of the existing party council with a smaller party executive, and the establishment of delegate voting at party conferences.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBurchell2000145_28-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBurchell2000145-28">&#91;28&#93;</a></sup> Many party members opposed the reforms, believing that they would undermine the internal party democracy, and amid the arguments various key members resigned or were dismissed from the Greens.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBurchell2000145–146_29-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBurchell2000145–146-29">&#91;29&#93;</a></sup> Although Green 2000 proposals were defeated at the party's 1990 conference, they were overwhelmingly carried at their 1991 conference, resulting in an internal restructuring of the party.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMcCulloch1992422_30-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMcCulloch1992422-30">&#91;30&#93;</a></sup> Between the end of 1990 and mid-1992, the party lost over half its members, with those polled indicating that frustration over a lack of clear and effective party leadership was a major reason in their decision.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBirch200968_31-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBirch200968-31">&#91;31&#93;</a></sup> The party fielded more candidates than it had ever done before in the <a href="/wiki/1992_United_Kingdom_general_election" title="1992 United Kingdom general election">1992 general election</a> but was widely deemed to have performed poorly.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTERootes199575_32-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTERootes199575-32">&#91;32&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In 1993, the party adopted its "Basis for Renewal" program in an attempt to bring together conflicting factions and thus save the party from bankruptcy and potential demise.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBurchell2000146_33-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBurchell2000146-33">&#91;33&#93;</a></sup> The party sought to escape their reputation as an environmentalist <a href="/wiki/Single-issue_party" class="mw-redirect" title="Single-issue party">single-issue party</a> by placing greater emphasis on social policies.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBurchell2000148_34-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBurchell2000148-34">&#91;34&#93;</a></sup>
Recognising their poor performance in the 1992 national elections, the party decided to focus on gaining support in local elections, targeting wards where there was a pre-existing support base of Green activists.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBurchell2000146_33-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBurchell2000146-33">&#91;33&#93;</a></sup> In 1993, future party leader and MP Lucas gained a seat on <a href="/wiki/Oxfordshire_County_Council" title="Oxfordshire County Council">Oxfordshire County Council</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTERootes199579Burchell2000146_35-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTERootes199579Burchell2000146-35">&#91;35&#93;</a></sup> with other gains following in the 1995 and 1996 local elections.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBurchell2000146_33-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBurchell2000146-33">&#91;33&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The Greens sought to build alliances with other parties in the hope of gaining representation at the parliamentary level.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBurchell2000147_36-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBurchell2000147-36">&#91;36&#93;</a></sup> In Wales, the Greens endorsed <a href="/wiki/Plaid_Cymru" title="Plaid Cymru">Plaid Cymru</a> candidate <a href="/wiki/Cynog_Dafis" title="Cynog Dafis">Cynog Dafis</a> in the 1992 general election, having worked with him on a number of environmental initiatives.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBurchell2000147_36-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBurchell2000147-36">&#91;36&#93;</a></sup> For the 1997 general election, the Ceredigion branch of the Greens endorsed Dafis as a joint Plaid Cymru/Green candidate, but this generated controversy with the party, with critics believing it improper to build an alliance with a party that did not share all of the Greens' views. In April 1995 the Green National Executive ruled that the party should withdraw from this alliance due to ideological differences.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBurchell2000147_36-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBurchell2000147-36">&#91;36&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>As the Labour Party shifted to the political centre under the leadership of <a href="/wiki/Tony_Blair" title="Tony Blair">Tony Blair</a> and his <a href="/wiki/New_Labour" title="New Labour">New Labour</a> project, the Greens sought to gain the support of the party's disaffected leftists.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBirch200955_37-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBirch200955-37">&#91;37&#93;</a></sup>
During the <a href="/wiki/1999_European_Parliament_election_in_the_United_Kingdom" title="1999 European Parliament election in the United Kingdom">1999 European Parliament elections</a>, the first to be held in the UK using <a href="/wiki/Proportional_representation" title="Proportional representation">proportional representation</a>, the Greens gained their first Members of the European Parliament (MEPs), Lucas (<a href="/wiki/South_East_England_(European_Parliament_constituency)" title="South East England (European Parliament constituency)">South East England</a>) and <a href="/wiki/Jean_Lambert" title="Jean Lambert">Jean Lambert</a> (<a href="/wiki/London_(European_Parliament_constituency)" title="London (European Parliament constituency)">London</a>).<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBurchell2000145,_149_38-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBurchell2000145,_149-38">&#91;38&#93;</a></sup> At the <a href="/wiki/2000_London_Assembly_election" title="2000 London Assembly election">inaugural London Assembly Elections in 2000</a>, the party gained 11% of the vote and returned three <a href="/wiki/Members_of_the_London_Assembly" class="mw-redirect" title="Members of the London Assembly">Assembly Members</a> (AM),<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBurchell2000149–150Birch200955_39-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBurchell2000149–150Birch200955-39">&#91;39&#93;</a></sup> and although this dropped to two following the <a href="/wiki/2004_London_Assembly_election" title="2004 London Assembly election">2004 London Assembly Elections</a>, the Green AMs proved vital in passing the annual budget of Mayor <a href="/wiki/Ken_Livingstone" title="Ken Livingstone">Ken Livingstone</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBirch200955_37-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBirch200955-37">&#91;37&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>At the <a href="/wiki/2001_United_Kingdom_general_election" title="2001 United Kingdom general election">2001 general election</a> they polled 0.7% of the vote and gained no seats.<sup id="cite_ref-40" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-40">&#91;40&#93;</a></sup> At the <a href="/wiki/2004_European_Parliament_election_in_the_United_Kingdom" title="2004 European Parliament election in the United Kingdom">2004 European Parliamentary elections</a> the party returned 2 MEPS the same as in 1999; overall, the Party polled 1,033,093 votes.<sup id="cite_ref-41" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-41">&#91;41&#93;</a></sup> In the <a href="/wiki/2005_United_Kingdom_general_election" title="2005 United Kingdom general election">2005 general election</a> the party gained over 1% of the vote for the first time, and polled over 10% in the constituencies of <a href="/wiki/Brighton_Pavilion_(UK_Parliament_constituency)" title="Brighton Pavilion (UK Parliament constituency)">Brighton Pavilion</a> and <a href="/wiki/Lewisham_Deptford_(UK_Parliament_constituency)" title="Lewisham Deptford (UK Parliament constituency)">Lewisham Deptford</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBirch200956_42-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBirch200956-42">&#91;42&#93;</a></sup> This growth has been attributed to the increasing public visibility of the party as well as a general growth in support for smaller parties in the UK.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBirch200956_42-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBirch200956-42">&#91;42&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span id="Caroline_Lucas_.282008.E2.80.932012.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Caroline_Lucas_(2008–2012)">Caroline Lucas (2008–2012)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Green_Party_of_England_and_Wales&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Caroline Lucas (2008–2012)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><div id="mwe_player_0" class="PopUpMediaTransform" style="width:220px;" videopayload="&lt;div class=&quot;mediaContainer&quot; style=&quot;width:640px&quot;&gt;&lt;video id=&quot;mwe_player_1&quot; <p>In November 2007, the party held an internal referendum to decide on whether it should replace its use of two "principal speakers", one male and the other female, with the more conventional roles of "leader" and "deputy leader"; the motion passed with 73% of the vote.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBirch200967_43-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBirch200967-43">&#91;43&#93;</a></sup> In September 2008, the party then elected its first leader, <a href="/wiki/Caroline_Lucas" title="Caroline Lucas">Caroline Lucas</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBirch200967_43-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBirch200967-43">&#91;43&#93;</a></sup> with <a href="/wiki/Adrian_Ramsay" title="Adrian Ramsay">Adrian Ramsay</a> elected deputy leader.<sup id="cite_ref-44" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-44">&#91;44&#93;</a></sup> In the party's first election with Lucas as leader, it retained both its MEPs in the <a href="/wiki/2009_European_Parliament_election_in_the_United_Kingdom" title="2009 European Parliament election in the United Kingdom">2009 European elections</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-45" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-45">&#91;45&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In the <a href="/wiki/2010_United_Kingdom_general_election" title="2010 United Kingdom general election">2010 general election</a>, the party returned its first <a href="/wiki/Member_of_Parliament#United_Kingdom" class="mw-redirect" title="Member of Parliament">Member of Parliament</a> (MP). Lucas was returned as MP for the seat of <a href="/wiki/Brighton_Pavilion_(UK_Parliament_constituency)" title="Brighton Pavilion (UK Parliament constituency)">Brighton Pavilion</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-46" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-46">&#91;46&#93;</a></sup> Following the election, <a href="/wiki/Keith_Taylor_(British_politician)" title="Keith Taylor (British politician)">Keith Taylor</a> succeeded her as MEP for South East England. They also saved their deposit in <a href="/wiki/Hove_(UK_Parliament_constituency)" title="Hove (UK Parliament constituency)">Hove</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Brighton_Kemptown_(UK_Parliament_constituency)" title="Brighton Kemptown (UK Parliament constituency)">Brighton Kemptown</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-47" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-47">&#91;47&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In the <a href="/wiki/2011_United_Kingdom_local_elections" title="2011 United Kingdom local elections">2011 local government elections in England and Wales</a>, the Green Party in Brighton and Hove took minority control of the <a href="/wiki/Brighton_and_Hove_City_Council" title="Brighton and Hove City Council">City Council</a> by winning 23 seats, 5 short of an overall majority.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (July 2015)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>
</p><p>At the <a href="/wiki/2012_United_Kingdom_local_elections" title="2012 United Kingdom local elections">2012 local government elections</a> the Green Party gained 5 seats, and retained both AMs at the <a href="/wiki/2012_London_Assembly_election" title="2012 London Assembly election">2012 London Assembly election</a>. At the <a href="/wiki/2012_London_mayoral_election" title="2012 London mayoral election">London Mayoral Election</a> the party's candidate <a href="/wiki/Jenny_Jones_(Green_politician)" class="mw-redirect" title="Jenny Jones (Green politician)">Jenny Jones</a> finished third, and lost her deposit.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (July 2015)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>
</p><p>In May 2012, Lucas announced that she would not seek re-election to the post of party leader.<sup id="cite_ref-48" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-48">&#91;48&#93;</a></sup> In September, <a href="/wiki/Natalie_Bennett" title="Natalie Bennett">Natalie Bennett</a> was elected party leader and <a href="/wiki/Will_Duckworth" title="Will Duckworth">Will Duckworth</a> deputy leader in the <a href="/wiki/2012_Green_Party_of_England_and_Wales_leadership_election" title="2012 Green Party of England and Wales leadership election">leadership election took place</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-new_leader_49-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-new_leader-49">&#91;49&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Guardian_new_leader_50-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Guardian_new_leader-50">&#91;50&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-51" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-51">&#91;51&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span id="Natalie_Bennett_.282012.E2.80.932016.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Natalie_Bennett_(2012–2016)">Natalie Bennett (2012–2016)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Green_Party_of_England_and_Wales&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Natalie Bennett (2012–2016)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/2013_United_Kingdom_local_elections" title="2013 United Kingdom local elections">2013 local government elections</a> saw overall gains of 5 seats. The Party returned representation for the first time on the councils of Cornwall, Devon, and Essex.
</p><p>At the <a href="/wiki/2014_United_Kingdom_local_elections" title="2014 United Kingdom local elections">local government elections the following year</a>, the Greens gained 18 seats overall.<sup id="cite_ref-52" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-52">&#91;52&#93;</a></sup> In London, the party won four seats, a gain of two, holding seats in <a href="/wiki/London_Borough_of_Camden" title="London Borough of Camden">Camden</a><sup id="cite_ref-53" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-53">&#91;53&#93;</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/London_Borough_of_Lewisham" title="London Borough of Lewisham">Lewisham</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-54" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-54">&#91;54&#93;</a></sup> and gaining seats in <a href="/wiki/London_Borough_of_Islington" title="London Borough of Islington">Islington</a><sup id="cite_ref-55" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-55">&#91;55&#93;</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/London_Borough_of_Lambeth" title="London Borough of Lambeth">Lambeth</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-56" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-56">&#91;56&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r889293853/mw-parser-output/.tmulti">.mw-parser-output .tmulti .thumbinner{display:flex;flex-direction:column}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .tmulti .text-align-center{text-align:center}@media all and (max-width:720px){.mw-parser-output .tmulti .thumbinner{width:100%!important;box-sizing:border-box;max-width:none!important;align-items:center}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .trow{justify-content:center}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .tsingle{float:none!important;max-width:100%!important;box-sizing:border-box;text-align:center}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .thumbcaption{text-align:center}}</style><div class="thumb tmulti tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:353px;max-width:353px"><div class="trow"><div class="tsingle" style="width:147px;max-width:147px"><div class="thumbimage"><a href="/wiki/File:Amelia_womack.jpg" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ee/Shahrah_ali.jpg/200px-Shahrah_ali.jpg" decoding="async" width="200" height="181" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ee/Shahrah_ali.jpg/300px-Shahrah_ali.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ee/Shahrah_ali.jpg/400px-Shahrah_ali.jpg 2x" data-file-width="744" data-file-height="672" /></a></div></div></div><div class="trow"><div class="thumbcaption" style="text-align:left;background-color:transparent"><a href="/wiki/Amelia_Womack" title="Amelia Womack">Womack</a> and <a href="/wiki/Shahrar_Ali" title="Shahrar Ali">Ali</a> were voted deputy leaders in 2014</div></div></div></div>
<p>At the <a href="/wiki/2014_European_Parliament_election_in_the_United_Kingdom" title="2014 European Parliament election in the United Kingdom">2014 European elections</a> The Green Party finished fourth, above the <a href="/wiki/Liberal_Democrats_(UK)" title="Liberal Democrats (UK)">Liberal Democrats</a>, winning over 1.2 million votes.<sup id="cite_ref-57" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-57">&#91;57&#93;</a></sup> The party increased its European Parliament representation, gaining one seat in the <a href="/wiki/South_West_England_(European_Parliament_constituency)" title="South West England (European Parliament constituency)">South West England</a> region.<sup id="cite_ref-58" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-58">&#91;58&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In September 2014, The Green Party held its biennial leadership elections. Incumbent leader Bennett ran uncontested and retained her status as party leader. The election also saw a change in the elective format for the position of deputy leader. The party opted to elect two, gender-balanced deputy leaders, instead of one. <a href="/wiki/Amelia_Womack" title="Amelia Womack">Amelia Womack</a> and <a href="/wiki/Shahrar_Ali" title="Shahrar Ali">Shahrar Ali</a> won the two positions, succeeding former deputy leader Duckworth.<sup id="cite_ref-59" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-59">&#91;59&#93;</a></sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Reliable_sources" title="Wikipedia:Reliable sources"><span title="The material near this tag relies on an unreliable source. Self-published source (blog) (May 2015)">unreliable source</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>
</p><p>The party announced in October 2014 that Green candidates would be standing for parliament in at least 75% of constituencies in the 2015 general election. In the 2010 general election, they contested roughly 50% of seats.<sup id="cite_ref-60" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-60">&#91;60&#93;</a></sup> Following its rapid increase in membership and support, the Green Party also announced it was targeting twelve key seats for the 2015 general election. These seats were its one current seat, <a href="/wiki/Brighton_Pavilion_(UK_Parliament_constituency)" title="Brighton Pavilion (UK Parliament constituency)">Brighton Pavilion</a>, held by Lucas since 2010; <a href="/wiki/Norwich_South_(UK_Parliament_constituency)" title="Norwich South (UK Parliament constituency)">Norwich South</a>, a Liberal Democrat seat where June 2014 polling put the Greens in second place behind Labour;<sup id="cite_ref-61" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-61">&#91;61&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Bristol_West_(UK_Parliament_constituency)" title="Bristol West (UK Parliament constituency)">Bristol West</a>, another Liberal Democrat seat, where they targeted the student vote; <a href="/wiki/St._Ives_(UK_Parliament_constituency)" class="mw-redirect" title="St. Ives (UK Parliament constituency)">St. Ives</a>, where they received an average of 18% of the vote in county elections; <a href="/wiki/Sheffield_Central_(UK_Parliament_constituency)" title="Sheffield Central (UK Parliament constituency)">Sheffield Central</a>; <a href="/wiki/Liverpool_Riverside_(UK_Parliament_constituency)" title="Liverpool Riverside (UK Parliament constituency)">Liverpool Riverside</a>; <a href="/wiki/Oxford_East_(UK_Parliament_constituency)" title="Oxford East (UK Parliament constituency)">Oxford East</a>; <a href="/wiki/Solihull_(UK_Parliament_constituency)" title="Solihull (UK Parliament constituency)">Solihull</a>; <a href="/wiki/Reading_East_(UK_Parliament_constituency)" title="Reading East (UK Parliament constituency)">Reading East</a>; and three more seats with high student populations - <a href="/wiki/York_Central_(UK_Parliament_constituency)" title="York Central (UK Parliament constituency)">York Central</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cambridge_(UK_Parliament_constituency)" title="Cambridge (UK Parliament constituency)">Cambridge</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Holborn_and_St._Pancras_(UK_Parliament_constituency)" class="mw-redirect" title="Holborn and St. Pancras (UK Parliament constituency)">Holborn and St. Pancras</a>, where leader Bennett stood as the candidate.<sup id="cite_ref-62" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-62">&#91;62&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In December 2014, The Green Party announced that it had more than doubled its overall membership from 1 January that year to 30,809.<sup id="cite_ref-twitter.com_63-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-twitter.com-63">&#91;63&#93;</a></sup> This reflected the increase seen in opinion polls in 2014, with Green Party voting intentions trebling from 2-3% at the start of the year, to 7-8% at the end of the year, on many occasions, coming in fourth place with <a href="/wiki/YouGov" title="YouGov">YouGov</a>'s national polls, ahead of the Liberal Democrats, and gaining over 25% of the vote with 18 to 24-year-olds.<sup id="cite_ref-64" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-64">&#91;64&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-65" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-65">&#91;65&#93;</a></sup> This rapid increase in support for the party is referred to by media as the "Green Surge".<sup id="cite_ref-66" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-66">&#91;66&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-67" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-67">&#91;67&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-68" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-68">&#91;68&#93;</a></sup> The hashtag "#GreenSurge" has also been popular on social media (such as Twitter) from Green Party members and supporters,<sup id="cite_ref-69" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-69">&#91;69&#93;</a></sup> and as of 15 January 2015<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Green_Party_of_England_and_Wales&amp;action=edit">&#91;update&#93;</a></sup>, the combined Green Party membership in the UK stood at 44,713; greater than the number of members of <a href="/wiki/UKIP" class="mw-redirect" title="UKIP">UKIP</a> (at 41,943), and the <a href="/wiki/Liberal_Democrats_(UK)" title="Liberal Democrats (UK)">Liberal Democrats</a> (at 44,576).<sup id="cite_ref-70" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-70">&#91;70&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Opinion_polling_for_the_2015_United_Kingdom_general_election" title="Opinion polling for the 2015 United Kingdom general election">Polling</a> subsequently fell back as the 2015 general election approached:<sup id="cite_ref-71" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-71">&#91;71&#93;</a></sup> a Press Association poll of polls on 3 April, for example, put the Greens fifth with 5.4%.<sup id="cite_ref-72" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-72">&#91;72&#93;</a></sup> However, membership statistics continued to surge with the party attaining 60,000 in England and Wales that April.
</p><p>In the <a href="/wiki/2015_United_Kingdom_general_election" title="2015 United Kingdom general election">2015 general election</a>, Lucas was re-elected in Brighton Pavilion with an increased majority, and while failing to gain any additional seats, the Greens received their highest-ever vote share (over 1.1 million votes), and increased their national share of the vote from 1% to 3.8%.<sup id="cite_ref-73" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-73">&#91;73&#93;</a></sup> Overnight, the membership numbers increased to over 63,000.<sup id="cite_ref-74" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-74">&#91;74&#93;</a></sup> However, they lost 9 out of their 20 seats on the Brighton and Hove council, losing minority control.<sup id="cite_ref-75" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-75">&#91;75&#93;</a></sup> Nationwide, the Greens increased their share of councillors, gaining an additional 10 council seats while failing to gain overall control of any individual council.<sup id="cite_ref-76" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-76">&#91;76&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On 15 May 2016 Bennett announced she would not be standing for re-election in the party's biennial <a href="/wiki/2016_Green_Party_of_England_and_Wales_leadership_election" title="2016 Green Party of England and Wales leadership election">leadership election</a> due to take place in the summer.<sup id="cite_ref-77" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-77">&#91;77&#93;</a></sup> Former leader Lucas and Work and Pensions Spokesperson Bartley announced two weeks later that they intended to stand for leadership as a <a href="/wiki/Job_sharing" title="Job sharing">job share</a> arrangement.<sup id="cite_ref-job_share_78-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-job_share-78">&#91;78&#93;</a></sup> Nominations closed at the end of June, with the campaign period taking place in July and voting period in August and the results announced at the party's Autumn Conference in Birmingham from 2–4 September. It was announced on 4 September that Lucas and Bartley would become the party's leaders in a job share.<sup id="cite_ref-79" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-79">&#91;79&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span id="Lucas_and_Bartley_.282016.E2.80.932018.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Lucas_and_Bartley_(2016–2018)">Lucas and Bartley (2016–2018)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Green_Party_of_England_and_Wales&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Lucas and Bartley (2016–2018)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Lucas first suggested "progressive pacts" to work on a number of issues including combating climate change and for electoral reform, following the results of the <a href="/wiki/2015_United_Kingdom_general_election" title="2015 United Kingdom general election">2015 general election</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-80" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-80">&#91;80&#93;</a></sup> She then reiterated the call alongside Bartley as they announced their plan to share the leadership of the party.<sup id="cite_ref-job_share_78-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-job_share-78">&#91;78&#93;</a></sup> Following the <a href="/wiki/2016_United_Kingdom_European_Union_membership_referendum" title="2016 United Kingdom European Union membership referendum">vote to leave</a> the <a href="/wiki/European_Union" title="European Union">European Union</a> in June 2016, Bennett published an open letter, calling for an "anti-Brexit alliance" potentially comprising <a href="/wiki/Labour_Party_(UK)" title="Labour Party (UK)">Labour</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Liberal_Democrats_(UK)" title="Liberal Democrats (UK)">Liberal Democrats</a> and <a href="/wiki/Plaid_Cymru" title="Plaid Cymru">Plaid Cymru</a> to stand in a future <a href="/wiki/2017_United_Kingdom_general_election" title="2017 United Kingdom general election">snap election</a> in English and Welsh seats.<sup id="cite_ref-81" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-81">&#91;81&#93;</a></sup> The Green Party stood in 457 seats in the 2017 general election, securing 1.6% of the overall vote, and an average of 2.2% in seats it stood in<sup id="cite_ref-82" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-82">&#91;82&#93;</a></sup> While a disappointing result after the 2015 success, this was still the second-best Green result in a general election, and <a href="/wiki/Brighton_Pavillion" class="mw-redirect" title="Brighton Pavillion">Brighton Pavillion</a> remained Green with an increased majority.
</p><p>On 30 May 2018, Lucas announced she would not seek re-election in the <a href="/wiki/2018_Green_Party_of_England_and_Wales_leadership_election" title="2018 Green Party of England and Wales leadership election">2018 Green Party of England and Wales leadership election</a> and would stand down as co-leader.<sup id="cite_ref-83" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-83">&#91;83&#93;</a></sup> On 1 June 2018 Bartley announced a co-leadership bid alongside <a href="/wiki/Si%C3%A2n_Berry" title="Siân Berry">Siân Berry</a>, former candidate for the Mayor of London in 2008 and 2016.<sup id="cite_ref-84" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-84">&#91;84&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span id="Bartley_and_Berry_.282018.E2.80.93.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Bartley_and_Berry_(2018–)">Bartley and Berry (2018–)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Green_Party_of_England_and_Wales&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Bartley and Berry (2018–)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Bartley and Berry were <a href="/wiki/2018_Green_Party_of_England_and_Wales_leadership_election" title="2018 Green Party of England and Wales leadership election">elected as co-leaders</a> in September 2018, winning 6,279 of 8,329 votes.<sup id="cite_ref-85" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-85">&#91;85&#93;</a></sup> In the 2019 local elections, the Green Party secured their best ever local election result, more than doubling their number of council seats from 178 to 372 councillors.<sup id="cite_ref-86" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-86">&#91;86&#93;</a></sup> This success was followed by a similarly successful European election where Greens won (including Scottish Greens and the Green Party in Northern Ireland) over two million votes for the first time since 1989, securing 7 MEPs, up from 3. This included winning seats for the first time in the East of England, North West England, West Midlands and Yorkshire &amp; the Humber, with <a href="/wiki/Magid_Magid" title="Magid Magid">Magid Magid</a> elected in the latter.<sup id="cite_ref-87" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-87">&#91;87&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Ideology_and_policy">Ideology and policy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Green_Party_of_England_and_Wales&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Ideology and policy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Welfare_Not_Warfare.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/ff/Welfare_Not_Warfare.jpg/220px-Welfare_Not_Warfare.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="209" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/ff/Welfare_Not_Warfare.jpg/330px-Welfare_Not_Warfare.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/ff/Welfare_Not_Warfare.jpg/440px-Welfare_Not_Warfare.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1071" data-file-height="1019" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Welfare_Not_Warfare.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>"Welfare not Warfare" sign, indicating the Green Party's policy towards social justice and non-violence</div></div></div>
<p>Sociologist Chris Rootes stated that the Green Party took "the left-libertarian" vote,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTERootes199576_88-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTERootes199576-88">&#91;88&#93;</a></sup> while Dennison and Goodwin characterised it as reflecting "libertarian-universalistic values".<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEDennisonGoodwin2015185_89-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEDennisonGoodwin2015185-89">&#91;89&#93;</a></sup> The party wants an end to "<a href="/wiki/Big_government" title="Big government">big government</a>" – which they see as hindering open and transparent democracy – and want to limit the power of "<a href="/wiki/Big_business" title="Big business">big business</a>" – which, they argue, upholds the unsustainable trend of globalisation, and is detrimental to local trade and economies.<sup id="cite_ref-gydg_90-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-gydg-90">&#91;90&#93;</a></sup> There have been allegations of factionalism and infighting in the Green Party between liberal, socialist, and anarchist factions.<sup id="cite_ref-91" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-91">&#91;91&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The Party publishes a full set of its policies, as approved by successive party conferences, collectively entitled "<i>Policies for a Sustainable Society</i>" (originally "<i>The Manifesto for a Sustainable Society</i>" before February 2010).<sup id="cite_ref-pss_92-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-pss-92">&#91;92&#93;</a></sup> This manifesto was summarised by <a href="/wiki/LGBT" title="LGBT">LGBT</a> and human rights campaigner <a href="/wiki/Peter_Tatchell" title="Peter Tatchell">Peter Tatchell</a> as "radical socialist", "incorporat[ing] key socialist values" as it "rejects privatisation, free-market economics and globalisation, and includes commitments to public ownership, workers' rights, economic democracy, progressive taxation and the redistribution of wealth and power".<sup id="cite_ref-93" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-93">&#91;93&#93;</a></sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template noprint Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:No_original_research#Primary,_secondary_and_tertiary_sources" title="Wikipedia:No original research"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable secondary sources. (May 2018)">non-primary source needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Manifesto">Manifesto</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Green_Party_of_England_and_Wales&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Manifesto">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<table class="box-Update plainlinks metadata ambox ambox-content ambox-Update" role="presentation"><tbody><tr><td class="mbox-image"><div style="width:52px"><img alt="Ambox current red.svg" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/98/Ambox_current_red.svg/42px-Ambox_current_red.svg.png" decoding="async" width="42" height="34" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/98/Ambox_current_red.svg/63px-Ambox_current_red.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/98/Ambox_current_red.svg/84px-Ambox_current_red.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="360" data-file-height="290" /></div></td><td class="mbox-text"><div class="mbox-text-span">This section needs to be <b>updated</b>.<span class="hide-when-compact"> Please update this article to reflect recent events or newly available information.</span>  <small class="date-container"><i>(<span class="date">May 2018</span>)</i></small></div></td></tr></tbody></table>
<p>The party publishes a manifesto for each of its election campaigns.<sup id="cite_ref-pss_92-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-pss-92">&#91;92&#93;</a></sup> In their 2015 Election Manifesto, for the <a href="/wiki/2015_United_Kingdom_general_election" title="2015 United Kingdom general election">2015 general election</a>, the Greens outlined many new policies, including a <a href="/wiki/Robin_Hood_tax" title="Robin Hood tax"><i>Robin Hood</i> tax</a> on banks, and a new 60% tax on those earning over £150,000.<sup id="cite_ref-94" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-94">&#91;94&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Economic_policy">Economic policy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Green_Party_of_England_and_Wales&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Economic policy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The Green Party believes in “an economy that works for all”. This includes radical steps to eliminate poverty with ambitious social policies such as increasing the <a href="/wiki/Minimum_wage" title="Minimum wage">Minimum wage</a> in line with <a href="/w/index.php?title=The_living_wage&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="The living wage (page does not exist)">the living wage</a>. They also want to introduce a four-day working week, many economists say this will result in stagnant economic growth while others say it would boost productivity and growth as Mondays and Fridays are the least productive days in the week.<sup id="cite_ref-95" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-95">&#91;95&#93;</a></sup> The Greens pledge to introduce a <a href="/wiki/Universal_Basic_Income" class="mw-redirect" title="Universal Basic Income">Universal Basic Income</a> which will give every adult (unemployed or not) at least 72 pounds a week, this is meant to incentivise the unemployed to find work and prepare Britain for a future with <a href="/wiki/Artificial_Intelligence" class="mw-redirect" title="Artificial Intelligence">Artificial Intelligence</a> dominated jobs. The Green Party want to raise <a href="/wiki/Corporation_tax" class="mw-redirect" title="Corporation tax">Corporation tax</a> from the current 19% to a higher amount, this is designed to generate more government revenue and insure large corporations do not become too powerful. The party wants to end subsidies for fossil fuels and replace them with subsidies for <a href="/w/index.php?title=Renewerable_energy&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Renewerable energy (page does not exist)">renewerable energy</a> sources such as Wind and Solar power. Investment In <a href="/wiki/Green_Energy" class="mw-redirect" title="Green Energy">Green Energy</a> could potentially create more jobs and boost the economy or result is stagnant growth. Environmental economic policy also includes a Green New deal that the Green Party say will generate new jobs and reduce Britains energy costs. The Green Party wants to increase Britain's development and its position on the <a href="/w/index.php?title=Human_Development_Idex&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Human Development Idex (page does not exist)">Human Development Idex</a> and <a href="/w/index.php?title=Free_time_index&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Free time index (page does not exist)">free time index</a>. They believe that uncontrolled economic growth has contributed to <a href="/wiki/Pollution" title="Pollution">Pollution</a> and <a href="/wiki/Global_Warming" class="mw-redirect" title="Global Warming">Global Warming</a> and that more steps should be taken to ensure that growth is sustainable and keeps environmental damage to a minimum.<sup id="cite_ref-96" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-96">&#91;96&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Environmental_policy">Environmental policy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Green_Party_of_England_and_Wales&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Environmental policy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The party states that it would phase out <a href="/wiki/Fossil_fuel" title="Fossil fuel">fossil fuel</a>-based power generation, and would work toward closing coal-fired power stations as soon as possible. The Green Party would also remove subsidies for nuclear power within ten years and work towards fazing out nuclear energy. The party aims for the UK to become carbon neutral. The Green Party Manifesto states:
</p><p>"The UK should base its future emissions budgets on the principles of science and equity and the aim of keeping global warming below 1.5 C. These principles entail the UK reducing its own emissions to net-zero by 2030 and seeking to reduce the emissions embedded in its imports to zero as soon as possible. The urgency of these objectives requires the UK to make overcoming the technological, political and social obstacles a national priority."<sup id="cite_ref-97" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-97">&#91;97&#93;</a></sup> The Green Party wants to set up an environmental protection committee to ensure the protection of habitats and to enhance biodiversity.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Foreign_policy_and_defence">Foreign policy and defence</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Green_Party_of_England_and_Wales&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Foreign policy and defence">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Since at least 1992, the party has emphasised unilateral <a href="/wiki/Nuclear_disarmament" title="Nuclear disarmament">nuclear disarmament</a> and called for the rejection of the <a href="/wiki/Trident_nuclear_programme" class="mw-redirect" title="Trident nuclear programme">Trident nuclear programme</a> of nuclear weapons in the <a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom" title="United Kingdom">United Kingdom</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTERootes199577_98-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTERootes199577-98">&#91;98&#93;</a></sup> To campaign for the latter measure it has teamed up with the <a href="/wiki/Campaign_for_Nuclear_Disarmament" title="Campaign for Nuclear Disarmament">Campaign for Nuclear Disarmament</a>, <a href="/wiki/Plaid_Cymru" title="Plaid Cymru">Plaid Cymru</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Scottish_National_Party" title="Scottish National Party">Scottish National Party</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-99" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-99">&#91;99&#93;</a></sup> Former Leader <a href="/wiki/Natalie_Bennett" title="Natalie Bennett">Natalie Bennett</a> has advocated replacing the UK Army with a "home defence force", according to <i><a href="/wiki/The_Daily_Telegraph" title="The Daily Telegraph">The Telegraph</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-100" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-100">&#91;100&#93;</a></sup> "In the long term," it would take the UK out of <a href="/wiki/NATO" title="NATO">NATO</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-101" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-101">&#91;101&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The party has opposed <a href="/wiki/2003_invasion_of_Iraq" title="2003 invasion of Iraq">2003 invasion of Iraq</a>, NATO-led <a href="/wiki/2011_military_intervention_in_Libya" title="2011 military intervention in Libya">military intervention in Libya</a><sup id="cite_ref-102" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-102">&#91;102&#93;</a></sup> and British involvement in <a href="/wiki/Saudi_Arabian-led_intervention_in_Yemen" title="Saudi Arabian-led intervention in Yemen">Saudi Arabian-led intervention in Yemen</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-103" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-103">&#91;103&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The party campaigns for the rights of indigenous people around the world and argues for greater <a href="/wiki/Autonomy" title="Autonomy">autonomy</a> for these individuals. Furthermore, they support the granting of compensation and justice for historical wrongs, and that the reappropriation of lands and resources should be granted to certain nations and peoples. The party also believes that the cancelling of <a href="/wiki/International_debt" class="mw-redirect" title="International debt">international debt</a> should take place immediately and any financial assistance should be in the form of grants and not loans, limiting debt service payments to 10% of export earnings per year.<sup id="cite_ref-gydg_90-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-gydg-90">&#91;90&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The Green Party advocate for a less "bully boy culture" from the <a href="/wiki/Western_world" title="Western world">Western world</a> and more self-sustainability in terms of food and energy policy on a global level, with aid only being given to countries as a last resort in order to prevent them from being indebted to their donors.<sup id="cite_ref-gydg_90-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-gydg-90">&#91;90&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Amid the toughening rhetoric surrounding immigration at the 2015 general election, the Greens issued mugs emblazoned with the slogan "Standing Up For Immigrants".<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEDennisonGoodwin2015184–185_104-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEDennisonGoodwin2015184–185-104">&#91;104&#93;</a></sup> They claimed to offer a "genuine alternative" to the views of the mainstream parties by promoting the removal of restrictions on the number of foreign students, abolishing rules on family migration, and promoting further rights for asylum seekers.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEDennisonGoodwin2015185_89-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEDennisonGoodwin2015185-89">&#91;89&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Drug_policy">Drug policy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Green_Party_of_England_and_Wales&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Drug policy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The Green Party has an official "Drugs Group", for drugs policy and research,<sup id="cite_ref-105" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-105">&#91;105&#93;</a></sup> and the party supports decriminalising the recreational use of <a href="/wiki/Cannabis" title="Cannabis">cannabis</a>, considering the drugs issue a health, rather than criminal issue.<sup id="cite_ref-106" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-106">&#91;106&#93;</a></sup>
Ian Barnett from the Green Party says that: "The Policy of 'War on Drugs' has clearly failed. We need a different approach towards the control and misuse of drugs." However, the party does aim to minimise drug use due to the negative effects on the individual and society at large.<sup id="cite_ref-107" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-107">&#91;107&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Sexual_orientation_and_gender_identity">Sexual orientation and gender identity</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Green_Party_of_England_and_Wales&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Sexual orientation and gender identity">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The sexual orientation and gender identity group within the party known as LGBTIQA+ Greens stated aim is to <a href="/wiki/Consciousness_raising" title="Consciousness raising">raise awareness</a> on <a href="/wiki/LGBT_rights_in_the_United_Kingdom" title="LGBT rights in the United Kingdom">LGBTIQA+ rights</a> and issues affecting the broader <a href="/wiki/LGBT_community" title="LGBT community">LGBTIQA+ community</a>, as well as broader <a href="/wiki/Green_politics" title="Green politics">Green politics</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-108" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-108">&#91;108&#93;</a></sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template noprint Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:No_original_research#Primary,_secondary_and_tertiary_sources" title="Wikipedia:No original research"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable secondary sources. (May 2018)">non-primary source needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>
</p><p>The 2015 and 2017 general election manifestos contained policies on all teachers to be trained on LGBTIQA+ issues (such as "providing mandatory <a href="/wiki/HIV" title="HIV">HIV</a>, sex, and relationships education – age appropriate and LGBTIQA+-inclusive – in all schools from primary level onwards"), to reform the system of pensions, of end the "spousal veto"<sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Manual_of_Style#Technical_language" title="Wikipedia:Manual of Style"><span title="The material near this tag may be using jargon that limits the article&#39;s accessibility. (May 2018)">jargon</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> and to "make equal marriage truly equal".<sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Manual_of_Style#Technical_language" title="Wikipedia:Manual of Style"><span title="The material near this tag may be using jargon that limits the article&#39;s accessibility. (May 2018)">jargon</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> Bennett has also voiced support for <a href="/wiki/Polygamy" title="Polygamy">polygamy</a> and <a href="/wiki/Polyamorous" class="mw-redirect" title="Polyamorous">polyamorous</a> relationships.<sup id="cite_ref-109" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-109">&#91;109&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The Green Party supports <a href="/wiki/Same-sex_marriage_in_England_and_Wales" class="mw-redirect" title="Same-sex marriage in England and Wales">same-sex marriage</a> and The Green Party group on <a href="/wiki/Brighton_and_Hove_City_Council" title="Brighton and Hove City Council">Brighton and Hove City Council</a> considered expelling a member (Christina Summers) in 2012 due to opposition to same-sex marriage legislation on religious grounds.<sup id="cite_ref-110" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-110">&#91;110&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-111" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-111">&#91;111&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Transport">Transport</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Green_Party_of_England_and_Wales&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Transport">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The Green party has called for "A People’s Transport System"<sup id="cite_ref-ReferenceA_112-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ReferenceA-112">&#91;112&#93;</a></sup> to help deal with the issues not just to the <a href="/wiki/Earth" title="Earth">planet</a> but to local communities as well. The Green Party has an official "Transport Working Group", aimed at helping to draw up policies to be voted on at conference. One of the flagship and long-standing policies in this field is returning the <a href="/wiki/British_Rail" title="British Rail">railways to public ownership</a><sup id="cite_ref-ReferenceA_112-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ReferenceA-112">&#91;112&#93;</a></sup> along with renationalising other forms of transport
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Governance">Governance</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Green_Party_of_England_and_Wales&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Governance">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Global_governance">Global governance</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Green_Party_of_England_and_Wales&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Global governance">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>The party campaigns for greater accountability in global governance, with the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations" title="United Nations">United Nations</a> made up of elected representatives and more regional representation, as opposed to the current nation-based setup. They want democratic control of the global economy with the <a href="/wiki/World_Trade_Organization" title="World Trade Organization">World Trade Organization</a>, <a href="/wiki/International_Monetary_Fund" title="International Monetary Fund">International Monetary Fund</a> and <a href="/wiki/World_Bank" title="World Bank">World Bank</a> reformed, democratised or even replaced. The party also wishes to prioritise social and environmental sustainability as a global policy.<sup id="cite_ref-gydg_90-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-gydg-90">&#91;90&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="National_governance">National governance</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Green_Party_of_England_and_Wales&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: National governance">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>The party advocates ending the <a href="/wiki/First_past_the_post_voting" class="mw-redirect" title="First past the post voting">first past the post voting</a> system for UK parliamentary elections and replacing it with a form of <a href="/wiki/Proportional_representation" title="Proportional representation">proportional representation</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBirch200965_113-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBirch200965-113">&#91;113&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The Green Party states that they believe there is "no place in government for the hereditary principle",<sup id="cite_ref-114" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-114">&#91;114&#93;</a></sup> while Bennett has said that she supports the abolition of the monarchy as the head of state, and fully supports <a href="/wiki/Republicanism_in_the_United_Kingdom" title="Republicanism in the United Kingdom">replacing the monarchy with a republic</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-115" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-115">&#91;115&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="European_Union">European Union</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Green_Party_of_England_and_Wales&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: European Union">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>The party supported <a href="/wiki/2016_United_Kingdom_European_Union_membership_referendum" title="2016 United Kingdom European Union membership referendum">the 2016 referendum</a> on the United Kingdom's membership of the European Union, calling it "a vital opportunity to create a more democratic and accountable Europe, with a clearer purpose for the future".<sup id="cite_ref-116" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-116">&#91;116&#93;</a></sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template noprint Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:No_original_research#Primary,_secondary_and_tertiary_sources" title="Wikipedia:No original research"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable secondary sources. (May 2018)">non-primary source needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> The party has criticised the <a href="/wiki/Common_Agricultural_Policy" title="Common Agricultural Policy">Common Agricultural Policy</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Common_Fisheries_Policy" title="Common Fisheries Policy">Common Fisheries Policy</a> and the "excessive influence" of the <a href="/wiki/European_Commission" title="European Commission">European Commission</a> in comparison to the <a href="/wiki/European_Council" title="European Council">European Council</a> and <a href="/wiki/European_Parliament" title="European Parliament">European Parliament</a>, describing it as "undemocratic and unaccountable".<sup id="cite_ref-Europe_policy_117-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Europe_policy-117">&#91;117&#93;</a></sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template noprint Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:No_original_research#Primary,_secondary_and_tertiary_sources" title="Wikipedia:No original research"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable secondary sources. (May 2018)">non-primary source needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>
The party favoured a "three yeses" approach to Europe: "yes to a referendum, yes to major EU reform and yes to staying in a reformed Europe". Bennett also added that:
</p>
<blockquote><p>'Yes to the EU' does not mean we are content with the union continuing to operate as it has in the past. There is a huge democratic deficit in its functioning, a serious bias towards the interests of neoliberalism and 'the market', and central institutions have been overbuilt. But to achieve those reforms we need to work with fellow EU members, not try to dictate high handedly to them, as David Cameron has done.<sup id="cite_ref-118" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-118">&#91;118&#93;</a></sup></p></blockquote>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Young_Greens">Young Greens</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Green_Party_of_England_and_Wales&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Young Greens">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Young_Greens_of_England_and_Wales" title="Young Greens of England and Wales">Young Greens of England and Wales</a></div>
<p>The youth wing of the Green Party, the Young Greens (of England and Wales), has developed independently from around 2002, and is for all Green Party members aged up to 30 years old. There is no lower age limit. The Young Greens have their own constitution, national committee, campaigns and meetings, and have become an active presence at Green Party Conferences and election campaigns. There are now many Young Greens groups on UK university, college and higher-education institution campuses. Many Green Party councillors are Young Greens, as are some members of GPEx and other internal party organs.<sup id="cite_ref-YGSite1_119-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-YGSite1-119">&#91;119&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Membership_and_finances">Membership and finances</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Green_Party_of_England_and_Wales&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Membership and finances">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<table class="box-Update plainlinks metadata ambox ambox-content ambox-Update" role="presentation"><tbody><tr><td class="mbox-image"><div style="width:52px"><img alt="Ambox current red.svg" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/98/Ambox_current_red.svg/42px-Ambox_current_red.svg.png" decoding="async" width="42" height="34" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/98/Ambox_current_red.svg/63px-Ambox_current_red.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/98/Ambox_current_red.svg/84px-Ambox_current_red.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="360" data-file-height="290" /></div></td><td class="mbox-text"><div class="mbox-text-span">This section needs to be <b>updated</b>.<span class="hide-when-compact"> Please update this article to reflect recent events or newly available information.</span>  <small class="date-container"><i>(<span class="date">May 2018</span>)</i></small></div></td></tr></tbody></table>
<p>According to accounts filed with the <a href="/wiki/Electoral_Commission_(United_Kingdom)" title="Electoral Commission (United Kingdom)">Electoral Commission</a>, for the year ending 31 December 2010 the party had an income of £770,495 with expenditure of £889,867.<sup id="cite_ref-soa-2010_120-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-soa-2010-120">&#91;120&#93;</a></sup>
Membership increased rapidly in 2014, more than doubling in that year.<sup id="cite_ref-greenparty.org.uk_121-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-greenparty.org.uk-121">&#91;121&#93;</a></sup> On 15 January 2015, the Green Party claimed that the combined membership of the UK Green parties (Green Party of England and Wales, <a href="/wiki/Scottish_Green_Party" title="Scottish Green Party">Scottish Green Party</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Green_Party_in_Northern_Ireland" title="Green Party in Northern Ireland">Green Party in Northern Ireland</a>) had risen to 43,829 members, surpassing <a href="/wiki/UKIP" class="mw-redirect" title="UKIP">UKIP</a>'s membership of 41,966, and making it the third-largest UK-wide political party in the UK in terms of membership.<sup id="cite_ref-BBC_News_15_January_2015_122-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BBC_News_15_January_2015-122">&#91;122&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-The_Independent_15_January_2015_123-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-The_Independent_15_January_2015-123">&#91;123&#93;</a></sup> On 14 January 2015, UK newspaper <i>The Guardian</i> had reported that membership of the combined UK Green Parties was closing on those of UKIP and the Liberal Democrats, but noted that it lagged behind that of the <a href="/wiki/Scottish_National_Party" title="Scottish National Party">Scottish National Party</a> (SNP), which has a membership of 92,187 members but is not a UK-wide party.<sup id="cite_ref-The_Guardian_14_January_2015_124-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-The_Guardian_14_January_2015-124">&#91;124&#93;</a></sup> Membership of the party peaked at over 67,000 members in the summer of 2015 after the general election, but has since declined subsequent to Jeremy Corbyn becoming leader of the Labour Party.<sup id="cite_ref-125" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-125">&#91;125&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
