</tbody></table>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Support_base">Support base</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Green_Party_of_England_and_Wales&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Support base">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="quotebox pullquote floatright" style="width:25em;&#32;;"><style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r887775652">.mw-parser-output .quotebox{background-color:#F9F9F9;border:1px solid #aaa;box-sizing:border-box;padding:10px;font-size:88%;max-width:100%}.mw-parser-output .quotebox.floatleft{margin:0.5em 1.4em 0.8em 0}.mw-parser-output .quotebox.floatright{margin:0.5em 0 0.8em 1.4em}.mw-parser-output .quotebox.centered{margin:0.5em auto 0.8em auto}.mw-parser-output .quotebox.floatleft p,.mw-parser-output .quotebox.floatright p{font-style:inherit}.mw-parser-output .quotebox-title{background-color:#F9F9F9;text-align:center;font-size:larger;font-weight:bold}.mw-parser-output .quotebox-quote.quoted:before{font-family:"Times New Roman",serif;font-weight:bold;font-size:large;color:gray;content:" “ ";vertical-align:-45%;line-height:0}.mw-parser-output .quotebox-quote.quoted:after{font-family:"Times New Roman",serif;font-weight:bold;font-size:large;color:gray;content:" ” ";line-height:0}.mw-parser-output .quotebox .left-aligned{text-align:left}.mw-parser-output .quotebox .right-aligned{text-align:right}.mw-parser-output .quotebox .center-aligned{text-align:center}.mw-parser-output .quotebox cite{display:block;font-style:normal}@media screen and (max-width:360px){.mw-parser-output .quotebox{min-width:100%;margin:0 0 0.8em!important;float:none!important}}</style>
<div class="quotebox-quote left-aligned" style="">"Green voters have tended to be younger and better educated than the electorate at large, and they are known to be more likely than most voters to work in the <a href="/wiki/Public_sector" title="Public sector">public sector</a>. In terms of values, Green voters have been found to be more often than not on the left of the political spectrum, and they have been more likely than the average voter to hold <a href="/wiki/Post-materialism" class="mw-redirect" title="Post-materialism">post-materialist</a> values, including support for environmental protection."</div>
<p><cite class="left-aligned" style="">— Sarah Birch, 2009<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBirch200961_139-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBirch200961-139">&#91;139&#93;</a></sup></cite>
</p>
</div>
<p>According to political scientist <a href="/wiki/Sarah_Birch" title="Sarah Birch">Sarah Birch</a>, the Green Party draws support from "a wide spectrum of the population".<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBirch200953_140-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBirch200953-140">&#91;140&#93;</a></sup>
In 1995, sociologist <a href="/w/index.php?title=Chris_Rootes&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Chris Rootes (page does not exist)">Chris Rootes</a> stated that the Green Party "appeals disproportionately to younger, highly educated professional people", although he noted that this support base was "not predominantly urban".<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTERootes199585_141-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTERootes199585-141">&#91;141&#93;</a></sup> In 2009, Birch noted that the Green's strongest areas of support were Labour-held seats in university towns or urban areas with relatively large student populations.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBirch200958–59_142-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBirch200958–59-142">&#91;142&#93;</a></sup> She noted that there were also strong correlations between areas of high Green support and high percentages of people who define themselves as having <a href="/wiki/Irreligion" title="Irreligion">no religion</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBirch200959–60_143-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBirch200959–60-143">&#91;143&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Birch noted that sociological polling revealed a "strong relationship" between individuals having voted for the <a href="/wiki/Liberal_Democrats_(UK)" title="Liberal Democrats (UK)">Liberal Democrats</a> in the past and holding favourable views of the Green Party, noting that the two groups were competing for "similar sorts of voters".<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBirch200964_144-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBirch200964-144">&#91;144&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Electoral_representation">Electoral representation</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Green_Party_of_England_and_Wales&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Electoral representation">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Green_Party_of_England_and_Wales_election_results" title="Green Party of England and Wales election results">Green Party of England and Wales election results</a></div>
<table align="right">

<tbody><tr>
<td><div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:352px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Green_representation_on_Borough-City-District_level_2019.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/37/Green_representation_on_Borough-City-District_level_2019.png/350px-Green_representation_on_Borough-City-District_level_2019.png" decoding="async" width="350" height="425" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/37/Green_representation_on_Borough-City-District_level_2019.png/525px-Green_representation_on_Borough-City-District_level_2019.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/37/Green_representation_on_Borough-City-District_level_2019.png/700px-Green_representation_on_Borough-City-District_level_2019.png 2x" data-file-width="1159" data-file-height="1407" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Green_representation_on_Borough-City-District_level_2019.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A map showing the representation of the Green Party of England and Wales at the Borough/City/District level of government, excluding Unitary Authorities (grey).</div></div></div>
</td>
<td><div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:352px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Green_Representation_on_English_and_Welsh_administrative_divisions_2019.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b2/Green_Representation_on_English_and_Welsh_administrative_divisions_2019.png/350px-Green_Representation_on_English_and_Welsh_administrative_divisions_2019.png" decoding="async" width="350" height="425" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b2/Green_Representation_on_English_and_Welsh_administrative_divisions_2019.png/525px-Green_Representation_on_English_and_Welsh_administrative_divisions_2019.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b2/Green_Representation_on_English_and_Welsh_administrative_divisions_2019.png/700px-Green_Representation_on_English_and_Welsh_administrative_divisions_2019.png 2x" data-file-width="1159" data-file-height="1407" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Green_Representation_on_English_and_Welsh_administrative_divisions_2019.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A map showing the representation of the Green Party of England and Wales at the County/Unitary Authority level of government.</div></div></div>
</td></tr></tbody></table>
<p>The party has one <a href="/wiki/House_of_Commons_of_the_United_Kingdom" title="House of Commons of the United Kingdom">Member of Parliament</a>, two Members of the <a href="/wiki/House_of_Lords" title="House of Lords">House of Lords</a>, seven Members of the <a href="/wiki/European_Parliament" title="European Parliament">European Parliament</a> and two Members of the <a href="/wiki/London_Assembly" title="London Assembly">London Assembly</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-145" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-145">&#91;145&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-146" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-146">&#91;146&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="House_of_Commons">House of Commons</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Green_Party_of_England_and_Wales&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: House of Commons">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p><a href="/wiki/Brighton_Pavilion_(UK_Parliament_constituency)" title="Brighton Pavilion (UK Parliament constituency)">Brighton Pavilion</a> was the Green Party's first and only parliamentary seat to date, won at the <a href="/wiki/2010_United_Kingdom_general_election" title="2010 United Kingdom general election">2010 general election</a> and held in <a href="/wiki/2015_United_Kingdom_general_election" title="2015 United Kingdom general election">2015</a> and <a href="/wiki/2017_United_Kingdom_general_election" title="2017 United Kingdom general election">2017</a>. As with other small parties, representation at the House of Commons has been hindered by the <a href="/wiki/First-past-the-post_voting" title="First-past-the-post voting">first-past-the-post</a> voting system.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTERootes199568Birch200956,_65_147-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTERootes199568Birch200956,_65-147">&#91;147&#93;</a></sup>
</p>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="House_of_Lords">House of Lords</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Green_Party_of_England_and_Wales&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: House of Lords">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The party's first <a href="/wiki/Life_peer" title="Life peer">life peer</a> was <a href="/wiki/Baron_Beaumont_of_Whitley" class="mw-redirect" title="Baron Beaumont of Whitley">Baron Beaumont of Whitley</a>, who left the Liberal Democrats and joined the Green Party in 1999. He sat as a Green until his death in 2008.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBirch200966_148-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBirch200966-148">&#91;148&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Baroness_Jones_of_Moulsecoomb" class="mw-redirect" title="Baroness Jones of Moulsecoomb">Baroness Jones of Moulsecoomb</a> became their next representative in the House of Lords, sitting alone until 2019.<sup id="cite_ref-149" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-149">&#91;149&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Natalie_Bennett" title="Natalie Bennett">Natalie Bennett</a> joined her in 2019 through <a href="/wiki/Theresa_May" title="Theresa May">Theresa May</a>'s resignation honour's list.<sup id="cite_ref-150" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-150">&#91;150&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="European_Parliament">European Parliament</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Green_Party_of_England_and_Wales&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: European Parliament">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Since the first UK election to the European Parliament with proportional representation, in <a href="/wiki/1999_European_Parliament_election_in_the_United_Kingdom" title="1999 European Parliament election in the United Kingdom">June 1999</a>, the Green Party of England and Wales has had representation in the European Parliament. From 1999 to 2010, the two MEPs were <a href="/wiki/Jean_Lambert" title="Jean Lambert">Jean Lambert</a> (London) and Lucas (South East England).  In 2010, on election to the House of Commons, Lucas resigned her seat and was succeeded by <a href="/wiki/Keith_Taylor_(British_politician)" title="Keith Taylor (British politician)">Keith Taylor</a>.  In <a href="/wiki/2014_European_Parliament_election_in_the_United_Kingdom" title="2014 European Parliament election in the United Kingdom">May 2014</a>, Taylor and Lambert held their seats, and were joined by <a href="/wiki/Molly_Scott_Cato" title="Molly Scott Cato">Molly Scott Cato</a> who was elected in the South West region, increasing the number of Green Party Members of the European Parliament to three for the first time.<sup id="cite_ref-151" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-151">&#91;151&#93;</a></sup> In <a href="/wiki/2019_European_Parliament_election_in_the_United_Kingdom" title="2019 European Parliament election in the United Kingdom">May 2019</a>, this number rose to seven: <a href="/wiki/Scott_Ainslie" title="Scott Ainslie">Scott Ainslie</a> (London), <a href="/wiki/Ellie_Chowns" title="Ellie Chowns">Ellie Chowns</a> (West Midlands), <a href="/wiki/Gina_Dowding" title="Gina Dowding">Gina Dowding</a> (North West England), <a href="/wiki/Magid_Magid" title="Magid Magid">Magid Magid</a> (Yorkshire and the Humber), <a href="/wiki/Alex_Phillips_(Green_politician)" class="mw-redirect" title="Alex Phillips (Green politician)">Alexandra Phillips</a> (South East England), <a href="/wiki/Catherine_Rowett" title="Catherine Rowett">Catherine Rowett</a> (East of England), and the re-elected Scott Cato.<sup id="cite_ref-152" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-152">&#91;152&#93;</a></sup>
</p>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Local_government">Local government</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Green_Party_of_England_and_Wales&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: Local government">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The party has representation at <a href="/wiki/Local_government_in_the_United_Kingdom" title="Local government in the United Kingdom">local government level</a> in England. The party has limited representation on most councils on which it is represented.
</p><p>From the early 1990s until 2009, the number of Green local councillors rose from zero to over 100<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBirch200956_42-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBirch200956-42">&#91;42&#93;</a></sup> and was in <a href="/wiki/Minority_government" title="Minority government">minority control</a> of <a href="/wiki/Brighton_and_Hove_City_Council" title="Brighton and Hove City Council">Brighton and Hove City Council</a> from <a href="/wiki/2011_Brighton_and_Hove_City_Council_election" title="2011 Brighton and Hove City Council election">2011</a> to <a href="/wiki/2015_Brighton_and_Hove_City_Council_election" title="2015 Brighton and Hove City Council election">2015</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-154" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-154">&#91;154&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-155" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-155">&#91;155&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>At the <a href="/wiki/2019_United_Kingdom_local_elections" title="2019 United Kingdom local elections">2019 United Kingdom local elections</a> a record number of Green Party candidates were elected, with many being the first Green candidates elected to their councils. The Party now has 372 councillors and is part of 9 council coalitions and supports a further coalition.
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Wales_Green_Party">Wales Green Party</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Green_Party_of_England_and_Wales&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28" title="Edit section: Wales Green Party">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Wales_Green_Party" title="Wales Green Party">Wales Green Party</a></div>
<p>The Wales Green Party (WGP; <a href="/wiki/Welsh_language" title="Welsh language">Welsh</a>: <i lang="cy">Plaid Werdd Cymru</i>) is a semi-<a href="/wiki/Autonomous_entity" class="mw-redirect" title="Autonomous entity">autonomous</a> <a href="/wiki/Political_party" title="Political party">political party</a> within the Green Party of England and Wales. It covers <a href="/wiki/Wales" title="Wales">Wales</a>, and is the only regional party with autonomous status within the GPEW. The WGP contests elections for the <a href="/wiki/National_Assembly_for_Wales" title="National Assembly for Wales">National Assembly for Wales</a> (as well as at the <a href="/wiki/Local_government_in_the_United_Kingdom" title="Local government in the United Kingdom">local</a>, <a href="/wiki/UK_Parliament" class="mw-redirect" title="UK Parliament">UK</a> and <a href="/wiki/European_Parliament" title="European Parliament">European</a> level) and has its own newsletters, membership list, <a href="/wiki/Annual_General_Meeting" class="mw-redirect" title="Annual General Meeting">AGMs</a> and <a href="/wiki/Manifesto" title="Manifesto">manifesto</a>. Members of the WGP are automatically members of the GPEW. Wales-wide decisions are taken by the Wales Green Party Council made up of the spokespeople, senior officers, and a representative from each local party.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Leadership">Leadership</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Green_Party_of_England_and_Wales&amp;action=edit&amp;section=29" title="Edit section: Leadership">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The Wales Green Party has always had its own spokesperson (now referred to as leader). Jake Griffiths became leader in 2009.<sup id="cite_ref-156" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-156">&#91;156&#93;</a></sup> Pippa Bartolotti was elected to succeed him in 2011, followed by Alice Hooker-Stroud from December 2015.<sup id="cite_ref-157" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-157">&#91;157&#93;</a></sup> Anthony Slaughter became deputy leader in 2014.<sup id="cite_ref-158" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-158">&#91;158&#93;</a></sup> Hooker-Stroud resigned in March 2017;<sup id="cite_ref-159" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-159">&#91;159&#93;</a></sup> the next leader was <a href="/w/index.php?title=Grenville_Ham&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Grenville Ham (page does not exist)">Grenville Ham</a>, whose Deputy Leaders were Benjamin Smith and Pippa Bartolotti.<sup id="cite_ref-160" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-160">&#91;160&#93;</a></sup> Ham left in October 2018 to join <a href="/wiki/Plaid_Cymru" title="Plaid Cymru">Plaid Cymru</a> after his proposal for Wales Green Party to become autonomous was voted down by members.<sup id="cite_ref-161" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-161">&#91;161&#93;</a></sup> The leader from December 2018 is Anthony Slaughter and his deputy is Duncan Rees.<sup id="cite_ref-162" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-162">&#91;162&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-163" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-163">&#91;163&#93;</a></sup>
Wales is represented internally within the GPEW by Chris Simpson and Chris Carmichael on the <a href="/wiki/Green_Party_of_England_and_Wales#Regional_Council" title="Green Party of England and Wales">Green Party Regional Council</a> (GPRC).  Both sets of positions are directly elected by <a href="/wiki/Postal_ballot" class="mw-redirect" title="Postal ballot">postal ballot</a>.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="History_2">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Green_Party_of_England_and_Wales&amp;action=edit&amp;section=30" title="Edit section: History">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The Green Parties in the United Kingdom have their roots in the PEOPLE movement which was founded in 1972. This became the Ecology Party three years later, and then the <a href="/wiki/Green_Party_(UK)" title="Green Party (UK)">Green Party</a> in 1985. Scotland, Wales and Northern Ireland each had separate branches. In 1990, the Scottish and Northern Irish branches left the UK Greens to form separate parties. The English and Welsh parties became the Green Party of England and Wales, with the Welsh branch being semi-autonomous.<sup id="cite_ref-164" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-164">&#91;164&#93;</a></sup> At the <a href="/wiki/1992_United_Kingdom_general_election" title="1992 United Kingdom general election">1992 general election</a>, local Greens entered an electoral alliance with <a href="/wiki/Plaid_Cymru" title="Plaid Cymru">Plaid Cymru</a> in the constituency of <a href="/wiki/Ceredigion_(UK_Parliament_constituency)" title="Ceredigion (UK Parliament constituency)">Ceredigion and Pembroke North</a>. The alliance was successful with <a href="/wiki/Cynog_Dafis" title="Cynog Dafis">Cynog Dafis</a> being returned in a surprise result as the <a href="/wiki/Member_of_Parliament" class="mw-redirect" title="Member of Parliament">MP</a>, defeating the <a href="/wiki/Liberal_Democrats_(UK)" title="Liberal Democrats (UK)">Liberal Democrat</a> incumbent by over 3,000 votes.<sup id="cite_ref-165" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-165">&#91;165&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-166" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-166">&#91;166&#93;</a></sup> The agreement broke down by 1995 following disagreement within the Welsh Green Party over endorsing another party's candidate, though Dafis would go on to serve in parliament as a Plaid Cymru member until 2000, and in the <a href="/wiki/National_Assembly_of_Wales" class="mw-redirect" title="National Assembly of Wales">National Assembly of Wales</a> from 1999 until 2003. Dafis later stated that he did not consider himself to be the "first Green MP".<sup id="cite_ref-167" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-167">&#91;167&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
